Jamison Brereton

4 (195)
Agni
Som─Бhuti Bh─Бrgava
9 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The hymn first concerns itself with the installation of the ritual fire (vss. 1тАУ3). There follows a naturalistic description, rich in metaphor and simile, of a fire first catching and then flaming up (vss. 4тАУ7). The hymn ends with two verses requesting benefits for the Gr╠еtsamada clan (8тАУ9). Oblique references to the myth of the recovery of the vanished fire in verses 2 and 9 provide the hymn with a larger ring-like structure.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Agni

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI invoke, on your behalf, the resplendent, the sinless Agni, the guest of mortals, the accepter of (sacrificial) food, who, knowing all that has been born, is like a friend, the supporter (of all beings) from men to gods.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I call for you upon the one of good brilliance, on Agni, the guest of the clans, who receives well-twisted (hymns), who receives very pleasurable offerings,
who, like an envoy, has become desirable to install as god among the god-directed people, as J─Бtavedas.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The stem suvс╣Ыkt├н- generally refers to a hymn and has in fact virtually been substantivized to mean hymn. However, it must be a bahuvr─лhi in origin; I generally tr. тАШhaving a good twistтАЩ, referring to the clever adornments, the turns of phrase, of a skillfully crafted hymn. Here I think it has two senses: first, characterizing Agni himself as тАШhaving a good twistтАЩ, perhaps referring to his swirling smoke and flames, but then, as a sort of secondary or double bahuvr─лhi, тАШhaving [/receiving] (hymns) with good twistsтАЩ. In this meaning it is parallel to supray├бsam тАШhaving [/receiving] pleasurable offeringsтАЩ. Note that the two are both final in their p─Бdas. I do not think GeldnerтАЩs тАЬeuren PreisтАЭ or RenouтАЩs тАЬhymne (incarn├й)тАЭ are either necessary or illuminating.

On the desiderative gerundive didhiс╣г─Б╠Бyya- see comm. ad I.73.2. Although the tr. тАЬdesirable to installтАЭ is somewhat heavy, the complexity of the formation seems to require a weighty tr.

The last p─Бda indulges in play with the name J─Бtavedas: dev├б ─Б╠Бdeve j├бne j─Бt├бved─Бс╕е. The first and last elements, dev├б тАж ved─Бс╕е, are virtual mirror images, with the 2nd word ─Б╠Бdeve reinforcing the first, and j├бne making an etymological figure with j─Бt├б.

Griffith

FOR you I call theglorious refulgent Agni, the guest of men, rich in oblations
Whom all must strive to win even as a lover, God among godly people, Jatavedas.

Oldenberg

I call for you Agni, shining with beautiful shine, praised with beautiful praise 1, the guest of the clans, the receiver of fine offerings, who is desirable like Mitra (or, like an ally), G├вtavedas the god, among godly people.

Ich rufe den sch├╢nleuchtenden Agni, euren Preis, den gutbek├╢stigten Gast der Clane, der wie ein Freund gewonnen werden mu├Я, der Gott unter dem g├╢tterfreundlichen Volke, der Jatavedas.

Grassmann

Ich rufe euren gl├дnzendsten, gepries’nen, den liebevollen Gast der Menschen, Agni; Den gern man sich wie einen Freund geneigt macht, den Wesenkenner, Gott bei Gott-ergebnen.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдм рдирд╡ рдЪрд╛рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рек рдЪрддреБрд░реНрде рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХрд╛ рдЖрд░рдореНрдн рд╣реИред рдЗрд╕рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердо рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рдЗрдордордЧреНрдирд┐рдВрд╡рд┐рдзрдиреНрддрдГ рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░рдиреНрддреЛрднреГрдЧрд╡реЛрд╕реНрдорддреНрдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЗрдорд╣рд░реНрд╖рдпрдГ рдЕрдкрд╛рдВрд╕рдзрд╕реНрдереЗрд╕рд╣рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗрдЖрдпреЛрд░реНрдордиреБрд╖реНрдп- рд╕реНрдпрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдпрд╕реНрд╡рднреВрддрд╛рд╕реБрд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖реБрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╕реНрд╡реГрддреНрд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖реБрддреЗрд╖рд╛рдореНрдордзреНрдпреЗрдЪрджреНрд╡рд┐рддрд╛рджреНрд╡рдпреЛрдГрд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рддреН рдЕрджрдзреБрдГ рдЕрдзрд╛рд░рдпрддреН рджрдзрд╛рддреЗ- рд░реНрд▓реБрдЩрд┐рд░реВрдкрдВ рдПрд╖реЛрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрднреВрдорднреВрдореНрдирд╛рдЕрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердВрд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рднреВрддрдЬрд╛рддрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдорджреНрд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдзреАрдиреНрдпрднреНрдпрд╕реНрддреБрдЕрднрд┐рднрд╡рддреБ рд╕рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдГ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдорд░рддрд┐рд░реАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдГ рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдореНрдордзреНрдпреЗрд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдВрдЕрд░рдгрд╢реАрд▓реЛрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдорджреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдореНрдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рддрдерд╛рдЬреАрд░рд╛рд╢реНрд╡рдГ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╢реНрд╡рдГ рее реи рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Bhс╣Ыgus, worshipping Agni, have twice made him manifest; (once) in the abode of the waters, and (once) among the sons of men; may that Agni, the sovereign of the gods, mounted on a rapid courser, ever overcome all (our foes).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Twice made him manifest: as lightning in the firmament, and as culinary fire on earth

Jamison Brereton

This one hereтАФhaving done honor (to him) in the seat of the watersтАФ once again the Bhr╠еgus have installed among the clans of ─Аyu.
Let him surmount all the worldsтАФAgni, the spoked wheel of the gods whose horses are lively.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The combination of honoring Agni тАЬin the seat of the watersтАЭ (a) and the Bhс╣Ыgus тАЬonce againтАЭ installing him among the clans (b) suggests that this vs. concerns the well-known myth of AgniтАЩs flight and concealment in the waters and the Bhс╣ЫgusтАЩ discovery, recovery, and reinstallation of Agni as the ritual fire. X.46.2 begins with a p─Бda identical to our p─Бda a and then relates the Bhс╣ЫguтАЩs finding of the fire g├║h─Б c├бtantam тАЬhiding in secretтАЭ: im├бс╣Г vidh├бnto ap─Б╠Бс╣Г sadh├бsthe, тАж pada├нr ├бnu gman / g├║h─Б c├бtantam u┼Ы├нjo n├бmobhir, ich├бnto dh─л╠Бr─Б bhс╣Ы╠Бgavo тАШvindan тАЬThis one here

– having done honor to him in the seat of the waters, they followed him along his tracks … / With reverences seeking him who was hiding in secret, the fire-priests, the insightful Bhrgus ╠е found him.тАЭ The same myth may be alluded to, in ring compositional fashion, in vs. 9 of our hymn. Note also that the poet to whom this hymn is ascribed is Som─Бhuti Bh─Бrgava.

02-03 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As Ian Hollenbaugh pointed out to me, dvit─Б╠Бdadhur in 2b can be read, contra Pp. adadhur, as dvit─Б╠Бdadhur, with perfect indic. or pres. injunc.; I now favor the unaugmented reading for reasons given below.

The contrast between the verbs in 2ab im├бm тАж (a)dadhur bhс╣Ы╠Бgavaс╕е and 3ab agn├нс╣Г dev─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАж dhuс╕е seems to encode the primal installation of Agni by the gods (3) and the recent installation, by men (2). Why the primal installation is expressed by a root aor. injunc. is not clear to me, but I would now alter the published translation to тАЬAgni did the gods install тАж,тАЭ from тАЬAgni have the gods installed тАж,тАЭ to reflect the remote past. Note also that the opening of 3b is metrically aberrant, with an opening of 3.

Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition suggest a rest in 4th position. It would be possible to restore *dadhuс╕е, which would match the same verb in the same position in 2b, but I think itтАЩs more likely that the omission of a syllable is meant to call attention to the difference in verb stems. A rest in 3rd position, producing a syncopated dhuс╕е might be better. If the two verbs are being directly contrasted, an unaugmented dadhur in 2 is more likely than augmented adadhur (in order to highlight the difference in stems). Discussion with Ian Hollenbaugh has helped me clarify my interpr.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gods, intending to dwell (in heaven), left, as a dear friend among the human races, that Agni, who, present in the chamber of sacrifice, is bounteous to the donor of offerings, and shines on the nights when he is wished for.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Shines on the nights: d─лdayad u┼Ыat─лr┼лrmya: u┼Ыat─лс╕е = k─Бmayam─Бn─Бс╕е, to be desired; ┼лrmy─Б r─Бtriс╕е = nights, all nights or the whole night: sarv─Бsu r─Бtriс╣гu d─лpyate; or, sarva r─Бtrir ─Бd─лpayati, he shines on all nights, or he lights up all nights

Jamison Brereton

Agni have the gods installed among the clans stemming from Manu, their own dear one, as those desiring to dwell peacefully (install)
an envoy.
He will shine toward the nights desirous (of him), he whose skill is to be besought for the one rich in gifts in (his own) house.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I tr. d─лdayat тАж ┼л╠Бrmy─Б ─Б╠БтАЬshine towards the nights,тАЭ rather than тАЬilluminate the nightsтАЭ with the standard tr., because I could not otherwise account for the ─Б╠Б. NartenтАЩs tr. (KlSch 370 n. 5) is similarly intransitive though with a temporal, rather than goal, acc.: тАЬEr soll die N├дchte hindurch leuchten.тАЭ Note mitr├бm тИЪdh─Б in b reprising the same lexeme in 1c.

On dakс╣г─Б╠Бyyaс╕е, whose morphology resembles didhiс╣г─Б╠Бyyaс╕е in 1c, see comm. ad I.91.3. As noted there, in this passage it could also or alternatively mean тАЬto be skillfully tended.тАЭ

02-03 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As Ian Hollenbaugh pointed out to me, dvit─Б╠Бdadhur in 2b can be read, contra Pp. adadhur, as dvit─Б╠Бdadhur, with perfect indic. or pres. injunc.; I now favor the unaugmented reading for reasons given below.

The contrast between the verbs in 2ab im├бm тАж (a)dadhur bhс╣Ы╠Бgavaс╕е and 3ab agn├нс╣Г dev─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАж dhuс╕е seems to encode the primal installation of Agni by the gods (3) and the recent installation, by men (2). Why the primal installation is expressed by a root aor. injunc. is not clear to me, but I would now alter the published translation to тАЬAgni did the gods install тАж,тАЭ from тАЬAgni have the gods installed тАж,тАЭ to reflect the remote past. Note also that the opening of 3b is metrically aberrant, with an opening of 3.

Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition suggest a rest in 4th position. It would be possible to restore *dadhuс╕е, which would match the same verb in the same position in 2b, but I think itтАЩs more likely that the omission of a syllable is meant to call attention to the difference in verb stems. A rest in 3rd position, producing a syncopated dhuс╕е might be better. If the two verbs are being directly contrasted, an unaugmented dadhur in 2 is more likely than augmented adadhur (in order to highlight the difference in stems). Discussion with Ian Hollenbaugh has helped me clarify my interpr.

Griffith

Among the tribes of men the Gods placed Agni as a dear Friend when they would dwell among them.
Against the longing nights may he shine brightly, and show the offerer in the house his vigour.

Oldenberg

The gods have established beloved Agni among the human clans as (people) going to settle (establish) Mitra 1. May he illuminate the nights that are longing (for him), he who should be treated kindly by the liberal (worshipper) in his house.

Geldner

Den Agni setzten die G├╢tter unter die menschlichen Clane ein als lieben Freund wie die, die in Frieden wohnen wollen, einen Mittler. Er erhellt die N├дchte, die nach ihm verlangen, der dem freigebigen Opferer in seinem Hause zur Gunst geneigt ist.

Grassmann

Den Agni setzten in der Menschen H├дuser als lieben Freund die G├╢tter, zur Erquickung; Er strahlte durch die holdgesinnten N├дchte; ihm muss im Haus der Gabenreiche dienen.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐рдГ рд░рдгреНрд╡рд╛рд░рдордгреАрдпрд╛рд╢рдмреНрджрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рд╡рд╛ рддрддреНрд░рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГтАФрд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд░рд┐рд╡рдпрдерд╛рд▓реЛрдХреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрд╛рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдореИрд░рдордгреАрдпрд╛рднрд╡рддрд┐рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдГрд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдиреАрдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ рдпрдерд╛рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╛рд░рдгреНрд╡рд╛рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рд╣рд┐рдпрд╛рдирд╕реНрдпрд╕рдореГрджреНрдзрд┐рдЩреНрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреЛрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рддреЛрдзрдХреНрд╖реЛрдГ рдХрд╛рд╖реНрдард╛рдиреН рджрд┐рдзрдХреНрд╖реЛрдГрджрдЧреНрдзреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫреЛрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ рд╕рдиреНрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ рд╕рдиреНрдж- рд░реНрд╢рдирд╛рд╡рд┐рд░реНрднрд╛рд╡реЛрдкрд┐рд░рдгреНрд╡рд╛ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реЛрд╖рдзреАрд╖реБрдХрд╛рд╖реНрдареЗрд╖реБрдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдЮреНрдЬреНрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛рдВ рдЬрд╛рддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╡рдЪрдирдВ рдЬреНрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рднрд░рд┐рднреНрд░рддреН рдЕрддреНрдп- рд░реНрдердВрд╡рд┐рд╣рд┐рд░рддрд┐рдХрдореНрдкрдпрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рд╣рд░рддреЗрд░реНрдпрдЩреН рд▓реБрдЧрдиреНрддрддреНрд╡реЗрдирджрд╛рдзрд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБрдирд┐рдкрд╛рддрд┐рддрд╛рд▓реНрд▓реЗрдЯреНрдпрдбрд╛рдЧрдордГ рдпрджреНрдпреЛрдЧрд╛рджрдирд┐- рдШрд╛рддрдГ рддрддреНрд░рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГтАФрд░рдереНрдпреЛрд░рдерд╛рд░реНрд╣реЛрд╜рддреНрдпреЛрди рд╡рд╛рдЬреАрдпрдерд╛ рд╡рд╛рд░рд╛рдиреН рджрдВрд╢рд╡рд╛рд░рдгрд╕рд╛рдзрдирд╛рдиреН рдмрд╛рд▓рд╛рдиреН рджреЛрдзрд╡реАрддрд┐ рдХрдореНрдкрдпрддрд┐рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдпреЛрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрдЬреНрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛рдГрдХрдореНрдкрдпрддрд┐ рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдГрдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГрд░рдгреНрд╡реЗрддрд┐ рее рек рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe cherishing of Agni is as agreeable as (the cherishing) of one’s self; (plural asant) is his appearance, when spreading abroad, and consuming (the fuel); he brandishes his flame among the bushes, as a chariot-horse lashes with his tail.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

His thriving, like oneтАЩs own, brings delight; delightful is his whole appearance when he is being urged on, about to burn.
He who is flicking his tongue hither and yon among the plants, like a steed at a chariot he keeps twitching his tail.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take d├бkс╣гu- as a pseudo-desid. u-participle; also dh├бkс╣гu- in X.115.4.

Because dodhav─лti in d is unaccented, it cannot be the verb of the relative clause beginning with y├бс╕е in c, despite the standard tr. Instead the intensive part.

Because of the equine simile and imagery, the primary reading of dodhav─лti v─Б╠Бr─Бn must be тАЬtwitches his tail(-hairs),тАЭ but a second reading тАЬshakes out choice thingsтАЭ is also invited.

Griffith

Sweet is his growth as of one’s own possessions; his look when rushing fain to burn is lovely.
He darts his tongue forth, like a harnessed courser who shakes his flowing tail, among the bushes.

Oldenberg

His prosperity is delightful as good pasture (?) 1; delightful is his appearance when the burning one is driven forward, he who quickly shaking his tongue among the plants waves 2 his tail mightily like a chariot-horse.

Geldner

Erfreulich ist sein Wachsen wie das des eigenen Besitzes, sein Anblick, wenn der Brennlustige sich in Lauf setzt, der in den Pflanzen z├╝ngelnd - wie ein Wagenro├Я sch├╝ttelt er seinen Schweif.

Grassmann

Wie eignes Gut sieht man ihn gerne wachsen, und liebt das Bild des brennenden, gesch├╝rten, Der zu den Pflanzen seine Zunge ausstreckt, der wie ein Wagenross die Schweife sch├╝ttelt.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрдГ) рдЬреЛ (рд░рдереНрдпрдГ) рд░рдереЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд (рдЕрддреНрдпрдГ) рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдд рддреБрд░рдЩреНрдЧ рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рдорд╛рди (рд╡рд░рд╛рдиреН) рдмрд╛рд▓рдХреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд▓реЛрдХреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдФрд░ (рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдореН) рдЕрдкрдиреА рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд╛ рдХреЛ (рджреЛрдзрд╡реАрддрд┐) рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдХрдореНрдкрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдФрд░ (рдУрд╖рдзреАрд╖реБ) рд╕реЛрдорд▓рддрд╛рджрд┐ рдФрд╖рдзреАрдпреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рд╡рд┐рднрд░рд┐рднреНрд░рддреН) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖ рдХрд░ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рди рд╣реИ рдЙрд╕ (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рдЗрд╕ рдХреА рд╣реБрдИ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпреЗрд╡) рдЕрдкрдиреА рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рджреВрд╕рд░реЗ рдХреА (рд░рдгреНрд╡рд╛) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдп (рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ) рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдзрд╛рддреБрд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рдФрд░ (рд╣рд┐рдпрд╛рдирд╕реНрдп) рд╡рджреНрдзрд┐ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рдЗрд╕ (рдзрдХреНрд╖реЛрдГ) рджрд╛рд╣ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдХреА (рд╕рдВрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдХрд░рдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реерекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдкреЛрд╖рдг рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХреА рдЬрд╛рддреА рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдФрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рднреА рдХрд░рдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗред рдЬреЛ рдЗрдиреНрдзрдиреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдмреЭрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдФрд░ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬрд▓рд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡рд╣ рд░рдереЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рд╢реАрдШреНрд░ рдЧрдорди рдХрд░рд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╡рдХреНрддрд╛ рдЕрдкрдиреА рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд╛ рдХреЛ рдХрдВрдкрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рднреВрдЧреЛрд▓реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдХрдВрдкрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИреерекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЛ рд░рдереНрдпреЛрд╜рддреНрдпреЛ рди рд╡рд╛рд░рд╛рдиреН рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдБрд╢реНрдЪ рджреЛрдзрд╡реАрддрд┐ред рдУрд╖рдзреАрд╖реБ рд╡рд┐рднрд░рд┐рднреНрд░рджрд╕реНрддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпреЗрд╡ рд░рдгреНрд╡рд╛ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд░реНрд╣рд┐рдпрд╛рдирд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдп рдзрдХреНрд╖реЛрдГ рд╕рдВрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд╢реНрдЪ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛ реерекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) (рд░рдгреНрд╡рд╛) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрд╛ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпреЗрд╡) (рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ) рдзрд╛рддреБрд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐рдГ (рд╕рдВрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ) рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреН рдкреНрд░реЗрдХреНрд╖рдгрдореН (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) (рд╣рд┐рдпрд╛рдирд╕реНрдп) рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдпред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрдирд╛рддреНрдордиреЗрдкрджрдореНред (рдзрдХреНрд╖реЛрдГ) рджрд╛рд╣рдХрд╕реНрдп (рд╡рд┐) (рдпрдГ) (рднрд░рд┐рднреНрд░рддреН) рднреГрд╢рдВ рдзрд░рдиреН (рдУрд╖рдзреАрд╖реБ) рд╕реЛрдорд▓рддрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ (рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдореН) (рдЕрддреНрдпрдГ) рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╕реНрддреБрд░рдЩреНрдЧрдГ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рд░рдереНрдпрдГ) рд░рдереЗрд╖реБ рд╕рд╛рдзреБрдГ (рджреЛрдзрд╡реАрддрд┐) рднреГрд╢рдВ рдХрдореНрдкрдпрддрд┐ (рд╡рд╛рд░рд╛рдиреН) рд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛рдирд┐рд╡ рд╡рд░рдгреАрдпрд╛рдиреН рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдиреН реерекрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhose greatness my colleagues loudly extol; who has manifested his real form to the priests; who is recognized at oblations by his variegated radiance, and who, though frequently growing old, again and again becomes young.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The formless mass [=smoke] of the wood-eater that they (first) marveled at to me, (that) color he changed as if for the fire-priests:
he is (now) perceived in delight with his bright light, he who, having grown old, in an instant has become young.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. describes the changes in color and form of the kindled fire as a sight to be wondered at. My tr. follows GeldnerтАЩs in outline and many details. The first sight is of the shapeless dark cloud of smoke (a), but that transforms into color and bright light (bc). On ├бbhva- see my forthcoming тАЬThe Blob in Ancient IndiaтАЭ (UCLA CMRS 2015 dragon conf. vol.), and for a parallel passage (also adduced by Geldner) VI.4.3 тАж y├бsya pan├бyanty ├бbhvam, bh─Б╠Бs─Бс╣Гsi vaste s┼л╠Бryo n├б ┼Ыukr├бh тАЬHe whose formless mass [=smoke] they [=mortals] marvel at тАж, he (then) clothes himself in lights, like the brilliant sun,тАЭ which seems to show parallel progress from dark to light and also contains a form of bh─Бs- as here.

van├бd- тАШwood-eaterтАЩ assumes a root noun 1st member v├бn-, preserved in a few forms such as loc. pl. v├бс╣Гsu (see Schindler, Rt. Noun), against the overwhelming number of forms to thematic v├бna-.

I do not understand the simile in b, u┼Ы├нgbhyo n├б тАЬas if for the fire-priests.тАЭ Perhaps the point is that the fire-tending performed by U┼Ыij-priests would cause the smoke to dissipate and the flames to appear, but that in their absence this change comes about anyway. Note that in X.46.2, quoted above ad vs. 2, the Bhс╣Ыgus seem to be identified as u┼Ы├нj-priests, so the simile here may be referring to ritual behavior in ancestral time. Witzel Got┼Н tr. тАЬwie den (danach) Verlangenden,тАЭ but u┼Ы├нj- is elsewhere the designation of a priest (and cf. Oldenberg Aves. usij-) and is so tr. by them elsewhere (e.g., I.60.4).

For r├бс╣Гsu as adverbial loc. pl. to the root noun r├бс╣З- see Schindler Rt. Noun and EWA, both s.v. raс╣З. And note raс╣Зv├б- in the preceding and following vss. (4a, 6c).

The last p─Бda describes the graying of the ash (тАЬhaving grown oldтАЭ) and then the rejuvenation of the flames presumably by the addition of more firewood.

Griffith

Since they who honour me have praised my greatness,-he gave, as ’twere, his hue to those who love him.
Known is he by his bright delightful splendour, and waxing old renews his youth for ever.

Oldenberg

When they praised 1 to me the monstrous might of the eater of the forests 2, he produced his (shining) colour as (he has done) for the Usigs 3. With shining splendour he has shone joyously, he who having grown old has suddenly become young (again).

Geldner

Was sie mir als unheimliche Erscheinung des Holzfeuers r├╝hmen, er hat diese Farbe wie f├╝r die Usij vertauscht. Er prangt in prangendem Glanz in Fr├╢hlichkeit, er der alt geworden alsbald jung wird.

Grassmann

Als meine Freunde angestaunt das Dunkel, verbarg er nicht den Heischenden sein Gl├дnzen; Mit hellem Lichte gl├дnzt er bei den Opfern, der alt geworden pl├╢tzlich wieder jung ward.

Elizarenkova

рдпреЛрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрд╡рдирд╛рд╡рдирд╛рдирд┐рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рд╕рдореВрд╣рд╛рдиреН рддрддреГрд╖рд╛рдгреЛрдирддреГрд╖рд┐рддрдЗрд╡ рддреНрд╡рд░рдорд╛рдгрдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рдЖрднрд╛рддрд┐рдЖрднрд╛рд╕рдпрддрд┐ рджрджрд╣- рддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рдирд╛рд╡рдиреЗрдЖрднрд╛рддрд┐ рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдгрдЙрджрдХрдорд┐рд╡ рдкрдерд╛рдкреНрд░рд╡рдгреЗрдирдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЗрдгрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдЗрддрд╕реНрддрддреЛрдЧрдЪреНрдЫ- рддрд┐ рд░рдереНрдпреЗрд╡рд░рдерд╕реНрдпрд╡реЛрдврд╛рд╢реНрд╡рдЗрд╡рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдиреАрддреН рд╢рдмреНрджрдпрддрд┐ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рд░рдерд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рддреН рд╕реЛрд░реНрдбреНрдпрд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГ рдпрдерд╛рд░рдереЛрдпреБрджреНрдзрдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЗрдгрдЧрдЪ- рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рд╕реНрд╡рдирддрд┐рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛рдзреНрд╡рд╛рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╡рд░реНрддреНрдорд╛ рддрдкреБрд╕реНрддрд╛рдкрдХрдГ рд░рдгреНрд╡реЛрд░рдордгреАрдпрдГ рдПрд╡рдореНрднреВрддрдГ рд╕рдиреН рдЪрд┐рдХреЗрддрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдп- рддреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рддрдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рдХрдЗрд╡ рдирднреЛрднрд┐рд░реНрдирдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░реИрдГ рд╕реНрдордпрдорд╛рдирдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдиреЛрджреНрдпреМрд░рд┐рд╡рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХрдЗрд╡ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдирднреЛрднрд┐рд░рдиреНрдд- рд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдкреНрд░рджреЗрд╢рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реИрдГ рд╕реНрдордпрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╢реЛрднрдорд╛рдиреЛрджреНрдпреМрд░рд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпрдЗрд╡рдиреАрд▓рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпреЛрдпрдерд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрддреЗрддрджреНрд╡рддреН рд╕реНрд╡рд╕рдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд░реЗрдгрдХреГрд╖реНрдгреАрднреВрддреЗрдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЗрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрддреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпрддрдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее рем рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho shines amidst the forests, as if satisfying himself (with food); who (rushes along), like water down a declivity, and thunders like a chariot (of war); dark-pathed consuming, yet delightful, he is regarded like the sky smiling with constellations.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who, (eating) wood like one athirst, shines here; like water along a path, like chariot (wheels) he has sounded.
Having a black road, red-hot, he appears bringing delight, smiling like heaven with its clouds [=his clouds of smoke].

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. take bh─Б╠Бti as the operator of the simile (e.g., Geldner тАЬDer nach den H├╢lzern ausschaut(?) wie der Durstige (nach Wasser)тАЭ), but this doesnтАЩt make much sense. From van├бd- тАШwood-eaterтАЩ in the immediately preceding vs. I extract тАШeatтАЩ to govern v├бn─Б and to be compared to t─Бtс╣Ыс╣г─Бс╣З├бс╕е тАШthirstingтАЩ in the same semantic realm, hence my тАЬ(eating) wood like one athirst.тАЭ My тАШred-hotтАЩ for t├бpuс╕е contrasts nicely with kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З─Б╠Бdhv─Б тАШhaving a black roadтАЩ, but is unfortunately not entirely legitimate: it is more literally just тАШhotтАЩ; there is no color component.

Act. pf. ciketa in c might be expected to mean тАШperceivesтАЩ, as generally, but it must mean instead тАШappearsтАЩ; so all the standard tr., and see also K├╝mmel (175) on the unusual sense. It is all the more surprising given med. cikite in the same meaning in the immediately preceding vs. (5c). But in this case the two forms may have been seen as metrical variants with identical sense, since ciketa is always p─Бda-final, cikite always post-caesura, as here.

The unexpressed concept in the simile тАЬlike heaven smiling with its cloudsтАЭ must be lightning, which smiles (I.168.8) or laughs (V.52.6). Lightning is white, like (some) clouds.

Griffith

Like one athirst, he lighteth up the forests; like water down the chariot ways he roareth.
On his black path he shines in burning beauty, marked as it were the heaven that smiles through vapour.

Oldenberg

He who shines on the forests 1 as if he were thirsty, who resounded like water on its path, like (the rattle of the wheels) of a chariot 2тАФhe whose path is black, the hot, the joyous one has shone, laughing 3 like the sky with its clouds.

Geldner

Der nach den H├╢lzern ausschaut wie der Durstige nach Wasser, er rauscht wie das Wasser auf seinem Wege, wie die Wagenr├дder, dessen Wege schwarz sind, der glutreiche, erfreuliche ist erprangt wie der Himmel, der durch die Wolken l├дchelt.

Grassmann

Der durstend gleichsam auf die Reiser hinstrahlt, wie Wasser rauschend auf der Fahrt, wie R├дder; Auf schwarzer Bahn erschien er gl├╝hend, lieblich, dem Himmel gleich, der durch die Wolken l├дchelt.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ (рд╡рдирд╛) рд╡рди рдФрд░ рдЬрд▓реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ (рддрддреГрд╖рд╛рдгрдГ) рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдкрд┐рдЖрд╕реЗ рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рдорд╛рди (рдЖ рднрд╛рддрд┐) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд┐рдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдФрд░ (рдкрдерд╛) рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рд╕реЗ (рд╡рд╛рдГ) рдЬрд▓ рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рдорд╛рди рддрдерд╛ (рд░рдереНрдпреЗрд╡) рд░рде рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдЬреЛ рд╣рд┐рдд рд╣реИ рдЙрд╕ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рд╕реЬрдХ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди (рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдиреАрддреН) рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рдпрдорд╛рди рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдЬреЛ (рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛рдзреНрд╡рд╛) рдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рд╡рд░реНрдгрдпреБрдХреНрдд (рддрдкреБрдГ) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ рддрдкрд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рд░рдгреНрд╡рдГ) рд░рдордгреАрдп (рд╕реНрдордпрдорд╛рдирдГ) рдХреБрдЫ рдореБрд╕реНрдХрд╛рддрд╛рд╕рд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ (рджреНрдпреМрд░рд┐рд╡) рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди (рдирднреЛрднрд┐рдГ) рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рджрд┐ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рдЪрд┐рдХреЗрдд) рдЙрджреНрдмреЛрдз рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрд╡рд▓рд┐рдд рд╣реЛ рд╡рд╣ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рд╣реА рдХреЛ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИ рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдХреЛрдИ рдЕрддрд┐рддреГрд╖рд╛рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдХрд╣рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдЬрди рд╣рдБрд╕рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рдХрд╣реЗ рдХрд┐ рдЬрд▓ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рдореЗрдВ рдЬрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╡рдирд╕реНрде рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдмрд╣реБрдд рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рдпрдорд╛рди рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЛ рд╡рдирд╛ рддрддреГрд╖рд╛рдгреЛ рдирд╛рднрд╛рддрд┐ рдкрдерд╛ рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдг рд░рдереНрдпреЗрд╡ рдЪ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдиреАрджреНрдпрдГ рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛рдзреНрд╡рд╛ рддрдкреВ рд░рдгреНрд╡рдГ рд╕реНрдордпрдорд╛рдиреЛ рджреНрдпреМрд░рд┐рд╡ рдирднреЛрднрд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдХреЗрдд рд╕ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рд░реЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддреБрдВ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдГ рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рдпрдГ) (рд╡рдирд╛) рд╡рдирд╛рдирд┐ (рддрддреГрд╖рд╛рдгрдГ) рднреГрд╢рдВ рддреГрдбреНрдпреБрдХреНрддрдГред рдЕрддреНрд░ рддреБрдЬрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рджрднреНрдпрд╛рд╕рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рднрд╛рддрд┐) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рддреЗ (рд╡рд╛рдГ) рдЙрджрдХрдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдкрдерд╛) рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЗрдг (рд░рдереНрдпреЗрд╡) рд░рдерд╛рдп рд╣рд┐рддреЗрд╡ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдиреАрддреН) рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рдпрддреЗ (рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛рдзреНрд╡рд╛) рдХреГрд╖реНрдгреЛрд╜рдзреНрд╡рд╛ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЛ рдпрд╕реНрдп (рддрдкреБрдГ) рдкрд░рд┐рддрд╛рдкрдХрдГ (рд░рдгреНрд╡рдГ) рд░рдордгреАрдпрдГ (рдЪрд┐рдХреЗрдд) рдЙрджреНрдмреБрдзреНрдпреЗрдд (рджреНрдпреМрд░рд┐рд╡) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╡рддреН (рд╕реНрдордпрдорд╛рдирдГ) рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪрд┐рджреНрдзрд╕рдиреНрдирд┐рд╡ (рдирднреЛрднрд┐рдГ) рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереИрдГ рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe who is in many plural ces, who spreads over the whole earth, like an animal without a herdsman, that goes according to its own will; Agni, the bright-shining, consuming the dry bushes, by whom the pain of blackness (is inflicted on the trees), entirely drinks up (their moisture).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He who has spread out, burning the broad (earth), like livestock without a herdsman he goes seeking his own way.
Agni, enflamed, scorching the brushwood, with his black wayward
course, has тАЬsweetened,тАЭ as it were, the ground.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The root тИЪsvad is generally a ritual technical term: the ritual fire тАЬsweetens,тАЭ that is, тАЬritually preparesтАЭ the oblations. Here the forest fire performs the same action on the non-ritual ground. Although this might depict some version of slash-and-burn agriculture (so Witzel Got┼Н), I think it more likely that the point is merely to give a ritual dimension to the wild and unpredictable actions of the forest fire, in the hope of exerting some control over it. The same sentiment is found in I.169.3 agn├н┼Ы cid dh├н с╣гm─Бtas├й ┼Ыu┼Ыukv─Б╠Бn, тАж d├бdhati pr├бy─Бс╣Гsi тАЬFor even a fire blazing in the brushwood can produce pleasurable offerings.тАЭ The position of n├б after the verb asvadayat in our passage suggests that the simile is targeting the verb, an extremely unusual situation in Vedic poetics.

Griffith

Around, consuming the broad earth, he wanders, free roaming like an ox without a herdsman,-
Agni refulgent, burning up the bushes, with blackened lines, as though the earth he seasoned.

Oldenberg

He who has spread himself burning over the wide (earth), moves about like an animal, free, without a keeper. The naming Agni, burning down the brushwood, with a black trail 1, has, as it were, tasted the earth.

Geldner

Der sich ausgebreitet hat ├╝ber die Erde hin brennend, er geht wie ein Tier ohne Hirten selbst seinen Weg suchend. Der flammende Agni, der das d├╝rre Holz verbrennt, hat auf seinen schwarzen Seitenwegen den Erdboden gleichsam zu seinem Mahle bereitet.

Grassmann

Er, der erstand, die Erde rings erhitzend, schweift frei umher wie hirtenlose Rinder, Mit Gluten Agni, das Gestr├╝pp versengend auf schwarzer Bahn, als koste er die Erde.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVerily, your praise has been recited (by us) at the third (daily) sacrifice, as it was in the repetition on your first propitiation; give us, Agni, ample and notorious food, posterity, riches, such as may be the support of numerous dependents.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Now, upon consideration of your previous help, a prayerful thought has been proclaimed to you at the third rite:
o Agni, grant to us a prize of an array of heroes, a lofty cattle-rich one, and wealth in good descendants.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The phrase tс╣Ыt─л╠Бye vid├бthe тАЬthird rite of distributionтАЭ probably refers to the Third Pressing (though the two other occurrences of тАЬthree vid├бthasтАЭ, at VI.51.2 and VII.66.10, do not seem to). Agni is of course present at all the pressings, but is not especially associated with the Third Pressing; however, tс╣Ыt─л╠Бye s├бvane at III.28.5 is in an Agni context.

Griffith

I, in remembrance of thine ancient favour have sung my hymn in this our third assembly.
O Agni, give us wealth with store of heroes and mighty strength in food and noble offspring.

Oldenberg

Now in the remembrance of thy former blessings this prayer has been recited to thee at the third sacrifice 1. Give to us, Agni, mighty strength with a succession of valiant men, with plenty of food; (give us) wealth with good progeny 2.

Geldner

Nun ward dir im Gedenken an fr├╝here Gunst bei dem dritten Opfer ein Gedicht vorgetragen. Gib uns, Agni, den hohen Siegerpreis von lauter S├╢hnen, von vielem Vieh, einen Schatz an guten Kindern!

Grassmann

Nun in Erinn’rung deiner alten H├╝lfe beim dritten Opfer ward Gebet gesprochen; Verlieh uns, Agni, heldenreiche, starke, ergieb’ge Nahrung, kinderreiche Habe.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBy you, (Agni), may the Gс╣Ыtsamadas, repeating your praise, become masters of the precious secret (treasures); so that they may be possessed of excellent dependents, and be able to resist (their) enemies; and do you give to (your) pious worshippers and to him who glorifies (you), such (abundant) food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

So that with you, o Agni, the Gr╠еtsamadas, gaining (the one deposited) in secret [=Agni], might surmount those below,
(the Gr╠еtsamadas) possessing good heroes and overcoming hostilityтАФ(so) establish this vital energy for the singer along with his patrons.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the published translation I supply with g├║h─Б a form like hit├бm (cf. I.23.14, II.11.5, IV.5.8, etc.), c├бrantam (III.1.9) or c├бtantam (I.65.1, X.46.2) referring to Agni when he was hiding in the waters, a myth I also think is referred to obliquely in vs. 2 of this hymn (see above). Our vs. 2 is especially close to X.46.2, which relates this story, and X.46.2c begins g├║h─Б c├бtantam (and continues with a ref. to the u┼Ы├нj-; see our 5b).

I therefore think my suggestion is justified, though I am usually reluctant to supply extraneous material. The point is – if the Gс╣Ыtsamadas (re)gain the hidden Agni, just as their ancestors the Bhс╣Ыgus did, they will get the upper hand against their enemies.

The standard tr. must construe g├║h─Б with vanv├бntaс╕е тАШgaining in secretтАЩ (e.g., Geldner тАЬheimlich ├╝berbieten und u├╝berwindenтАЭ). Although this is the obvious way to construe the text as given, the notion that our side would win by stealth and secret means seems antithetic to the Rigvedic ideal of combat, whether on the battlefield or the ritual ground. The adverb g├║h─Б is extremely common in the flight-of-Agni myth and in an Agni hymn would likely call to mind the whole story. I would now be inclined to emend the published translation to тАЬ(the one hiding) in secret,тАЭ not тАЬ(тАж deposited) in secret,тАЭ because of its apparent dependence on X.46.2 or a passage like it.

Griffith

May the Grtsamadas, serving in secret, through thee, O Agni, overcome their neighbours,
Rich in good heroes and subduing foemen. That vital power give thou to chiefs and singers.

Oldenberg

Give, O Agni, such vigour to thy praiser together with his liberal (lords), that the Gritsamadas, rich in valiant men, victorious over hostile plots, attaining (their aim) in secret, may overcome through thee (their rivals) who get behind 1.

Geldner

Auf das die Gritsamada┬┤s durch dich, Agni, die Nebenbuhler heimlich ├╝berwinden, sie die Meister, die die Gegner bezwingen - dazu gib dem S├дnger und zugleich den freigebigen G├╢nnern die Kraft!

Grassmann

O Agni, dass durch dich die Gritsamader die Nachbarn heimlich ├╝berfl├╝geln, siegreich, An Helden reich die Gegner ├╝berwindend, den Segen schenk den F├╝rsten und den S├дngern.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛) (рдпрдерд╛) рдпреЗрди рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг (рдЧреГрддреНрд╕рдорджрд╛рд╕рдГ) рдЧреГрддреНрд╕рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рдВ рдордж рдЖрдирдиреНрдж рдЗрд╡рд╛рдирдиреНрджреЛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдиреНрддреЗ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рдкрд╛рд╡рдХ рдЗрд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди (рдЧреБрд╣рд╛) рдЧреБрд╣рд╛рдпрд╛рдореН (рд╡рдиреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ) рд╡рд┐рднрдЬрдиреНрддрдГ (рдЙрдкрд░рд╛рдиреН) рдореЗрдШрд╛рдиреН (рдЕрднрд┐) (рд╕реНрдпреБрдГ) рднрд╡реЗрдпреБрдГ (рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░рд╛рд╕рдГ) рд╕реБрд╢реЛрднрдорд╛рдиреИрд░реНрд╡реАрд░реИрд░реНрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рдЕрднрд┐рдорд╛рддрд┐рд╕рд╛рд╣рдГ) рдпреЗрд╜рднрд┐рдорд╛рддрд┐рдиреН рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рд╕рд╣рдиреНрддреЗ (рд╕реНрдорддреН) рдПрд╡ (рд╕реВрд░рд┐рднреНрдпрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднреНрдпрдГ (рдЧреГрдгрддреЗ) рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рддрддреН) (рд╡рдпрдГ) рдХрд╛рдордореН (рдзрд╛рдГ) рджрдзрд╛рддрд┐ реерепрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпрдерд╛рд╜рд╜рдкреНрддреЗрднреНрдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднреНрдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рдЧреГрд╣реАрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЖрдирдиреНрджрд┐рддрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛ рд╡реАрд░рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдвреНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрд╛ рдЬрдирд╛ рдЬрд╛рдпрдиреНрддреЗ рддрдерд╛рд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдпрд╛ рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдЗрд╡ рджреБрдГрдЦрдВ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ реерепрее ред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдореН рее рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдердВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рд╣реЗ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреЛ! рдЬрд╕реЗ рдЖрдкреНрдд рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдХрдбреВрди рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдг рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░реВрди рдЖрдирдВрджреА, рд╡рд┐рдЬрдпреА рд╡реАрд░ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдп рдмрдирддрд╛рдд рд╡ рдЬрд╕рд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЕрдВрдзрдХрд╛рд░ рдирд╖реНрдЯ рдХрд░рддреЛ рддрд╕реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреЗрдиреЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рдЪрд╛ рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд. рее реп рее
